Finitude of Parts Demands a Specifier
First exposition: from finite parts to necessity of a specifier

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the world's composition from finite parts entails its finitude and the necessity of a specifier for its specific measure.

Core Idea
Finitude demands a specifier; equality in possibility requires an external selector.

Imam Nasafi begins his refutation by analyzing the world's composition. Since every part of the world is finite in essence, the whole cannot be infinite. Moreover, the world's specific size—among equally possible sizes—cannot be self-caused but requires a specifier. This argument establishes a key foundation for the world's contingency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the premise about parts
Read the first sentence: 'Every part of it is finite in essence.' This is the starting point of the argument.
The 'it' refers to the world (or body).
2
Follow the logical consequence
Understand that a whole composed of finite parts cannot be infinite. Imam Nasafi says that if it were possible, the world could be infinite in all directions, which is false.
This refutes materialist claims of an infinite universe.
3
Grasp the need for a specifier
The world has a specific measure, but other measures are equally possible. Since no inherent merit distinguishes one measure, a specifier (mukhassis) is required to select it.
This step introduces the concept of a specifier for contingent things.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كل جزء منه متناهي الذات، وخروج ما اجتمع من الأجزاء المتناهية عن المتناهي في الذات محال، ولو جاز ذا لجاز كون العالم غير متناه في جميع الجهات كما يزعم أهل الدهر وذلك باطل، ولأنه لابد من القول بالتناهي إذا وجد العالم لا في ذاته فبقى هو بذاته من العالم بجهة من الجهات ضرورة استحالة كون الباري جل وعلا مداخلا أجزاء العالم، وإذا ثبت تناهيه ثبت كونه على قدر مخصوص جميع مع كون غيره من الأقدار مساويا له في الجواز، واختصاص أحد الجائزين لن يثبت إلا بمخصص، إذ لا مزية له بذاته على ما يساويه في الجواز – والتقرير الثاني - أن ما كان متبعضا متجزئا لابد من أن يكون طويلا أو عريضا أو طويلا عريضا وهو السطح أو طويلا عريضا عميقا وهو المكعب، ثم إذا كان كذلك، لابد من أن يكون مدورا أو مثلثا أو مربعا أو مخمسا أو مسدسا أو مسبعا أو مثمنا أو غير ذلك مما يطول ذكره، فبعد ذلك إما أن يكون على هذه الأشكال أجمع فيكون مدورا مثلثا مربعا إلخ ذلك، وإما أن يكون على شكل من هذه الأشكال ولا جائز أن يكون على الأشكال كلها لما فيها من التناهي والتضاد، ولو جاز ذا في الغائب مع امتناعه في الشاهد لجاز في الغائب اجتماع الحركة والسكون والسواد والبياض والاجتماع والافتراق وحيث يبطل هذا بطل الأول لاستوائهما في الاستحالة في الشاهد فلم يبق إلا أنه على شكل من هذه الأشكال، وهيئة من هذه الهيئات، ولا مزية لما اختص به على غيره بما يساويه من الأشكال في الجواز، فبعد ذلك إما أن يقال إنما اختص بالثبوت من الأشكال الأخرى اختص لا بتخصيص مخصص، ولو جاز ذا لجاز في العالم، ولم يثبت دليل حدوثه، وافتقاره إلى صانع أوجده، وقد أقمنا الدلالة على إبطاله، وخصماؤنا في هذه المسألة ساعدونا على ذلك. وإما أن يقال بأنه اختص بذلك بتخصيص مخصص. ولو كان كذلك لكان محدثا محلا لقبول قدرة الغير وهو محال، إذ لو كان محدثا، لكان له محدث وكذا الكلام في الثاني والثالث إلى ما لا يتناهى والقول ببطلان ذلك قد مر، فثبت أن القول بكونه جسما يؤدي إلى القول بقدم العالم وتعطيل الصانع، أو إلى القول بحدوث الصانع وذلك محال وكل قول يؤدي إلى المحال فهو محال
Every part of it is finite in essence, and the emergence of what is composed of finite parts from the finite in essence is impossible. If this were permissible, it would be permissible for the world to be infinite in all directions as the materialists claim, and that is false. And because it is necessary to affirm finitude when the world exists not in its essence, so it remains itself from the world in one direction, due to the impossibility of the Exalted Creator being intermingled with the parts of the world. And when its finitude is established, its being upon a specific measure is established, together with other measures being equal to it in possibility. And the specification of one of the two possible things is not established except by a specifier, since it has no excellence by its essence over what is equal to it in possibility. – The second exposition: That which is partitioned and divisible must necessarily be long or wide or long and wide which is a surface, or long, wide, and deep which is a cube. Then, when it is like that, it must necessarily be round or triangular or square or pentagonal or hexagonal or heptagonal or octagonal or other than that which would be lengthy to mention. Then after that, either it is upon all these shapes together, so it would be round, triangular, square, etc., or it is upon one of these shapes. It is not possible that it be upon all shapes because of the finitude and contradiction in them. And if this were permissible in the unseen while it is impossible in the witnessed, then it would be permissible in the unseen for motion and rest, blackness and whiteness, coming together and separation, to coexist. And since this is invalid, the first is invalid because they are equal in impossibility in the witnessed. So nothing remains except that it is upon one of these shapes and one of these configurations. And there is no excellence for what it is specified with over other shapes that are equal to it in possibility. Then after that, either it is said that it was specified with existence over the other shapes without specification by a specifier. If this were permissible, it would be permissible for the world, and the proof of its temporal origination and its need for a Maker who brought it into existence would not be established, and we have already provided the proof of its invalidity, and our opponents in this issue have agreed with us on that. Or it is said that it was specified with that by the specification of a specifier. If it were like that, it would be originated, a locus for accepting the power of another, which is impossible. For if it were originated, it would have an originator, and likewise the discourse in the second and third ad infinitum. And the statement of the invalidity of that has already passed. So it is established that the statement that it is a body leads to the statement of the pre-eternity of the world and the negation of the Maker, or to the statement of the temporal origination of the Maker, and that is impossible. And every statement that leads to the impossible is itself impossible.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage presents a complex multi-step argument against the claim that the world (or by extension, the Creator) is a body. The author, Imam Nasafi, begins by establishing that the world is composed of finite parts, and the aggregation of finite parts cannot produce an infinite whole (as the materialists claim). Since the Creator is not intermingled with the world, the world must be finite in size, and hence has a specific dimension. Then he presents a second exposition (التقرير الثاني): anything that is divisible must have length, width, etc., and thus must have a specific shape (round, square, etc.). It cannot have all shapes simultaneously due to contradiction, so it must have one specific shape. Now, among all possible shapes, there is no inherent excellence in one over another, so the specification to one shape requires a specifier (مخصص) – a cause that selects it. If we say the specification happens without a specifier, that would apply to the world itself, undermining the proof of its contingency and need for a Creator – but even the opponents agree that is false. If we say it is due to a specifier, then that specifier would be originated (محدث) and subject to another's power, leading to an infinite regress, which is also impossible. Therefore, the claim that the world is a body leads to either the pre-eternity of the world (denying the Creator) or the origination of the Creator (impossible), so the original claim is impossible. The author follows the logical structure: hypothesis leads to absurdity, hence hypothesis is false.

Key Terms

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Even with finite parts, the whole could be infinite if parts are infinitely many.
Correction: Imam Nasafi argues that the whole emerging from finite parts cannot exceed the finite in essence; infinite is impossible.

The Shape Argument Leads to Absurdity
Second exposition: shape requirement and its absurd consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the requirement of shape for a body forces the necessity of a specifier for shape, and how this leads to either pre-eternity of the world or origination of the Creator, both impossible.

Core Idea
If the world were a body, its shape would require a specifier, leading to an infinite regress or absurdity.

In the second exposition, Imam Nasafi considers the implication that a divisible body must have a specific shape. Since all shapes are equally possible, the actual shape demands a specifier. If no specifier is invoked, the world would be self-subsistent, denying its need for a Creator. If a specifier is invoked, that specifier would itself be originated, leading to an infinite regress. Thus, the claim that the world is a body is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Understand that a body must have a shape
Read the beginning of the passage: anything divisible must be long, wide, deep, etc., and thus take a specific shape (round, square, etc.).
Shapes mentioned are examples; the point is any body has some shape.
2
See the need for a specifier for shape
Among all possible shapes, the actual shape has no intrinsic superiority. Therefore, a specifier is needed to choose it.
This mirrors the specifier argument for measure.
3
Examine the two alternatives
If the specifier is denied, the world could exist without a Creator, which is false. If a specifier is affirmed, that specifier would be originated and need another specifier, leading to infinite regress.
Both alternatives are impossible, so the original assumption is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كل جزء منه متناهي الذات، وخروج ما اجتمع من الأجزاء المتناهية عن المتناهي في الذات محال، ولو جاز ذا لجاز كون العالم غير متناه في جميع الجهات كما يزعم أهل الدهر وذلك باطل، ولأنه لابد من القول بالتناهي إذا وجد العالم لا في ذاته فبقى هو بذاته من العالم بجهة من الجهات ضرورة استحالة كون الباري جل وعلا مداخلا أجزاء العالم، وإذا ثبت تناهيه ثبت كونه على قدر مخصوص جميع مع كون غيره من الأقدار مساويا له في الجواز، واختصاص أحد الجائزين لن يثبت إلا بمخصص، إذ لا مزية له بذاته على ما يساويه في الجواز – والتقرير الثاني - أن ما كان متبعضا متجزئا لابد من أن يكون طويلا أو عريضا أو طويلا عريضا وهو السطح أو طويلا عريضا عميقا وهو المكعب، ثم إذا كان كذلك، لابد من أن يكون مدورا أو مثلثا أو مربعا أو مخمسا أو مسدسا أو مسبعا أو مثمنا أو غير ذلك مما يطول ذكره، فبعد ذلك إما أن يكون على هذه الأشكال أجمع فيكون مدورا مثلثا مربعا إلخ ذلك، وإما أن يكون على شكل من هذه الأشكال ولا جائز أن يكون على الأشكال كلها لما فيها من التناهي والتضاد، ولو جاز ذا في الغائب مع امتناعه في الشاهد لجاز في الغائب اجتماع الحركة والسكون والسواد والبياض والاجتماع والافتراق وحيث يبطل هذا بطل الأول لاستوائهما في الاستحالة في الشاهد فلم يبق إلا أنه على شكل من هذه الأشكال، وهيئة من هذه الهيئات، ولا مزية لما اختص به على غيره بما يساويه من الأشكال في الجواز، فبعد ذلك إما أن يقال إنما اختص بالثبوت من الأشكال الأخرى اختص لا بتخصيص مخصص، ولو جاز ذا لجاز في العالم، ولم يثبت دليل حدوثه، وافتقاره إلى صانع أوجده، وقد أقمنا الدلالة على إبطاله، وخصماؤنا في هذه المسألة ساعدونا على ذلك. وإما أن يقال بأنه اختص بذلك بتخصيص مخصص. ولو كان كذلك لكان محدثا محلا لقبول قدرة الغير وهو محال، إذ لو كان محدثا، لكان له محدث وكذا الكلام في الثاني والثالث إلى ما لا يتناهى والقول ببطلان ذلك قد مر، فثبت أن القول بكونه جسما يؤدي إلى القول بقدم العالم وتعطيل الصانع، أو إلى القول بحدوث الصانع وذلك محال وكل قول يؤدي إلى المحال فهو محال
Every part of it is finite in essence, and the emergence of what is composed of finite parts from the finite in essence is impossible. If this were permissible, it would be permissible for the world to be infinite in all directions as the materialists claim, and that is false. And because it is necessary to affirm finitude when the world exists not in its essence, so it remains itself from the world in one direction, due to the impossibility of the Exalted Creator being intermingled with the parts of the world. And when its finitude is established, its being upon a specific measure is established, together with other measures being equal to it in possibility. And the specification of one of the two possible things is not established except by a specifier, since it has no excellence by its essence over what is equal to it in possibility. – The second exposition: That which is partitioned and divisible must necessarily be long or wide or long and wide which is a surface, or long, wide, and deep which is a cube. Then, when it is like that, it must necessarily be round or triangular or square or pentagonal or hexagonal or heptagonal or octagonal or other than that which would be lengthy to mention. Then after that, either it is upon all these shapes together, so it would be round, triangular, square, etc., or it is upon one of these shapes. It is not possible that it be upon all shapes because of the finitude and contradiction in them. And if this were permissible in the unseen while it is impossible in the witnessed, then it would be permissible in the unseen for motion and rest, blackness and whiteness, coming together and separation, to coexist. And since this is invalid, the first is invalid because they are equal in impossibility in the witnessed. So nothing remains except that it is upon one of these shapes and one of these configurations. And there is no excellence for what it is specified with over other shapes that are equal to it in possibility. Then after that, either it is said that it was specified with existence over the other shapes without specification by a specifier. If this were permissible, it would be permissible for the world, and the proof of its temporal origination and its need for a Maker who brought it into existence would not be established, and we have already provided the proof of its invalidity, and our opponents in this issue have agreed with us on that. Or it is said that it was specified with that by the specification of a specifier. If it were like that, it would be originated, a locus for accepting the power of another, which is impossible. For if it were originated, it would have an originator, and likewise the discourse in the second and third ad infinitum. And the statement of the invalidity of that has already passed. So it is established that the statement that it is a body leads to the statement of the pre-eternity of the world and the negation of the Maker, or to the statement of the temporal origination of the Maker, and that is impossible. And every statement that leads to the impossible is itself impossible.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage presents a complex multi-step argument against the claim that the world (or by extension, the Creator) is a body. The author, Imam Nasafi, begins by establishing that the world is composed of finite parts, and the aggregation of finite parts cannot produce an infinite whole (as the materialists claim). Since the Creator is not intermingled with the world, the world must be finite in size, and hence has a specific dimension. Then he presents a second exposition (التقرير الثاني): anything that is divisible must have length, width, etc., and thus must have a specific shape (round, square, etc.). It cannot have all shapes simultaneously due to contradiction, so it must have one specific shape. Now, among all possible shapes, there is no inherent excellence in one over another, so the specification to one shape requires a specifier (مخصص) – a cause that selects it. If we say the specification happens without a specifier, that would apply to the world itself, undermining the proof of its contingency and need for a Creator – but even the opponents agree that is false. If we say it is due to a specifier, then that specifier would be originated (محدث) and subject to another's power, leading to an infinite regress, which is also impossible. Therefore, the claim that the world is a body leads to either the pre-eternity of the world (denying the Creator) or the origination of the Creator (impossible), so the original claim is impossible. The author follows the logical structure: hypothesis leads to absurdity, hence hypothesis is false.

هيئة
مخصص
محدث
قدم العالم
حدوث الصانع

Misconception: One might think that infinite regress is acceptable or that a specifier could be uncreated.
Correction: The argument shows infinite regress is impossible, and the specifier cannot be uncreated because it would then be subject to another's power, making it originated.

If God Were Composite: Non-Self-Subsisting Parts
Nasafi argues that composite parts must be self-subsisting or else creation is impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the assumption that God is composite leads to the absurd conclusion that creation is impossible if the parts are not self-subsisting.

Core Idea
Composition requires self-subsisting parts; otherwise the whole cannot exist.

Nasafi continues his argument against tajsim by showing that if God were composed of parts, each part must either be self-subsisting or not. If not, the whole cannot be self-subsisting, making the creation of the world impossible. This logical dilemma is the foundation of the second proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the literal translation. Notice how the argument is structured as a conditional: 'if He were composite, then...'
The passage is a single logical chain.
2
Identify the two possibilities
The passage presents two possibilities regarding the parts: either each part is self-subsisting (qā'im bi-dhātihī) or not. Locate where this distinction is made.
The first possibility is dismissed immediately as impossible.
3
Understand the consequence
If parts are not self-subsisting, the whole cannot be self-subsisting, so God would not be self-subsisting, making creation impossible. Ask yourself why creation from a non-self-subsisting being is impossible.
This is a key premise in the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الثاني، وهو أن القول بما قالوا يؤدي إلى إبطال دلالة التوحيد فهو أنه تعالى لو كان مؤتلفا متبعضا متجزئا لكان كل جزء منه قائما بنفسه إذ الائتلاف على ما لا قيام له بذاته محال، ولأن كل جزء منه لو لم يكن له قيام بذاته لاستحال أن يكون للكل قيام بذاته، فما ذا كل ذاته لا قيام له بذاته، ووجود تخليق العالم ممن لا قيام له بذاته محال، ولو كان كل جزء منه قائما بذاته فإما أن كان كل جزء منه موصوفا بصفات الكمال كالحياة والعلم والقدرة والسمع والبصر والإرادة، وإما أن لم يكن موصوفا بها، بل كان الموصوف بها جزء واحدا منه أو بعض الأجزاء دون البعض، فإن لم يكن كل جزء منها موصوفا بصفات الكمال لكان موصوفا بأضدادها من صفات النقص، كالموت والجهل والعجز والصمم والعمى والاضطرار، إذ ما كان قائما بذاته لا يستحيل عليه قبول صفات الكمال باعتبار ذاته، إذ كل قائم بالذات يجوز قبوله للصفات، وما لا يقوم به إنما لا يقوم لقيام ضده به. ولو كان موصوفا بصفات النقص لكان محدثا، فإذا ما لا يوصف من أجزائه بكونه حيا قادرا عالما سميعا بصيرا فهو محدث لقيام دليل الحدوث به، وكون أجزاء القديم محدثة محال، وإن كان كل جزء منه موصوفا بصفات الكمال فكان كل جزء حيا قادرا عالما سميعا بصيرا لكان كل جزء منه موصوفا بصفات الربوبية، فيكون القول به قولا بآلهة كثيرة، ويلزمون بعد ذلك ما مر من دلائل التوحيد، فإن كانت تلك الدلائل صحيحة كان القول بالتجسيم باطلا، وإن كانت تلك الدلائل فاسدة، كان القول بوحدانية الصانع باطلا، وقد ثبت وحدانية الصانع بالدلائل الموجبة للعلم الثابت على طريق التيقن، فكان القول بالتجسيم باطلا. وجاء من هذا أن من قال بأن الصانع جسم فقد أبطل التوحيد في الذات، ولا يقال إن حياة الباري وقدرته وعلمه أزلية، ولم يثبت فيها صفات الكمال ولم يدل على حدوثها، لأنا بينا أن القائم بالذات لا يستحيل قبوله الصفات، فكان امتناع قبول كل جزء منه صفات الكمال لقيام أضدادها من النقائص، فأما الصفات فيستحيل قبولها للصفات لذاتها لا لقيام صفة البعض بها، فلم يلزم بامتناع قبولها صفات الكمال أن تكون موصوفة بصفات النقص التي هي أمارات الحدث، وفيما نحن فيه الأمر بخلافه، والله الموفق.
As for the second [proof], which is that the statement according to what they said leads to the nullification of the indication of tawhid – it is that if He, exalted, were composed, divided into parts, and divisible, each part of Him would be self-subsisting, because composition from what is not self-subsisting is impossible; and because if each part of Him were not self-subsisting, it would be impossible for the whole to be self-subsisting, so then the whole essence would not be self-subsisting, and the existence of the creation of the world from one who is not self-subsisting is impossible. And if each part of Him were self-subsisting, then either each part of Him is described with attributes of perfection such as life, knowledge, power, hearing, sight, and will, or it is not described with them, but rather only one part or some parts are described with them and not others. If not every part is described with attributes of perfection, then it would be described with their opposites from attributes of deficiency, such as death, ignorance, incapacity, deafness, blindness, and constraint – because that which is self-subsisting is not by its essence impossible to receive attributes of perfection, for every self-subsisting entity may receive attributes, and that which does not receive them only does not receive them because its opposite is present in it. And if it were described with attributes of deficiency, it would be contingent; therefore, whatever of its parts is not described as being living, powerful, knowing, hearing, seeing is contingent due to the evidence of contingency applying to it, and it is impossible for parts of the Eternal to be contingent. And if each part of Him is described with attributes of perfection, so that each part is living, powerful, knowing, hearing, seeing, then each part would be described with attributes of lordship, and so the statement about Him would be a statement about many gods. And after that they incur what has passed of the proofs of tawhid: if those proofs are correct, then the statement of tajsim is false; and if those proofs are corrupt, then the statement of the oneness of the Maker is false. And the oneness of the Maker has been established by proofs that necessitate certain knowledge in a way of certainty, so the statement of tajsim is false. And from this it follows that whoever says that the Maker is a body has nullified tawhid in the essence. And let it not be said that the life, power, and knowledge of the Creator are eternal, and He has not proven attributes of perfection to be established in them nor has it indicated their contingency – because we have shown that the self-subsisting is not impossible to receive attributes; so the prevention of each part of Him from receiving attributes of perfection is due to the existence of their opposites from deficiencies. As for the attributes, it is impossible for them to receive attributes by their essence, not due to the existence of an attribute in some of them; so from the impossibility of their receiving attributes of perfection, it does not follow that they are described with attributes of deficiency which are signs of contingency. And in our case, the matter is otherwise. And God is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is a proof against tajsim (anthropomorphism) presented by Nasafi. He begins by stating the second argument: that the claim of the anthropomorphists leads to nullifying the evidence for tawhid (divine unity). The argument proceeds by analyzing the hypothetical consequences if God were composite (mu'talif, mutabaddid, mutajazzi'). Nasafi argues that if God were composed of parts, each part would either be self-subsisting or not. If a part were not self-subsisting, then the whole could not be self-subsisting, making the creation of the world by such a being impossible. If each part is self-subsisting, then there are two possibilities: either every part is described with attributes of perfection (life, knowledge, power, etc.) or not. If some parts lack these attributes, they must possess their opposites (death, ignorance, etc.), which are signs of contingency (huduth). Hence those parts would be contingent, and it is impossible for parts of the Eternal to be contingent. If, on the other hand, every part is described with attributes of perfection, then each part possesses lordship (rububiyya), leading to polytheism. Thus, the claim of tajsim contradicts the established proofs of God's oneness. Nasafi then addresses a potential objection: that God's attributes (life, power, knowledge) are eternal and not proven to be attributes of perfection or contingency. He replies that the impossibility of a self-subsisting entity receiving attributes can only be due to the presence of opposite deficiencies; but for the attributes themselves (as distinct from the essence), it is impossible for them to receive attributes by their very nature. Therefore, the objection does not apply, and the argument stands. He concludes with 'And God is the grantor of success.'

Key Terms
تجسيم (tajsim)
قائم بذاته (self-subsisting)
ائتلاف (composition)
تخليق (creation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The whole would still be self-subsisting.
B) The creation of the world would be impossible.
C) The part would be eternal.
D) The part would have attributes of perfection.

Key Takeaway
If God were composite, each part must be self-subsisting; otherwise, creation becomes impossible.

If God Were Composite: The Dilemma of Attributes
Nasafi demonstrates that assuming self-subsisting parts leads to either polytheism or contingency, thereby refuting tajsim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the destructive dilemma that faces anyone who claims God is composite: either each part has attributes of perfection leading to polytheism, or some lack them leading to contingency – both contradict tawhid.

Core Idea
A composite god either leads to many gods or to contingent parts.

Having established that parts of a composite god must be self-subsisting, Nasafi now examines two possibilities: either each part is described with attributes of perfection (life, knowledge, power, etc.) or not. Both lead to contradictions – either polytheism or contingency – thereby refuting tajsim. He then addresses a potential objection regarding God's eternal attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice that this passage continues from the previous one, starting with 'And if each part of Him were self-subsisting, then either...'
The passage contains a clear dichotomy.
2
Trace the two branches
Identify the two branches: (1) each part has attributes of perfection, (2) not. For each branch, note the consequence: perfection leads to many lords (polytheism); deficiency leads to contingency. Both are impossible for God.
Attributes of perfection include life, knowledge, power, hearing, sight, will.
3
Understand the objection and reply
Nasafi anticipates an objection: God's attributes are eternal, so how can they be signs of contingency? He replies that the impossibility of receiving attributes is due to the presence of opposites, but attributes themselves cannot receive attributes; thus the objection fails.
This shows the sophistication of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الثاني، وهو أن القول بما قالوا يؤدي إلى إبطال دلالة التوحيد فهو أنه تعالى لو كان مؤتلفا متبعضا متجزئا لكان كل جزء منه قائما بنفسه إذ الائتلاف على ما لا قيام له بذاته محال، ولأن كل جزء منه لو لم يكن له قيام بذاته لاستحال أن يكون للكل قيام بذاته، فما ذا كل ذاته لا قيام له بذاته، ووجود تخليق العالم ممن لا قيام له بذاته محال، ولو كان كل جزء منه قائما بذاته فإما أن كان كل جزء منه موصوفا بصفات الكمال كالحياة والعلم والقدرة والسمع والبصر والإرادة، وإما أن لم يكن موصوفا بها، بل كان الموصوف بها جزء واحدا منه أو بعض الأجزاء دون البعض، فإن لم يكن كل جزء منها موصوفا بصفات الكمال لكان موصوفا بأضدادها من صفات النقص، كالموت والجهل والعجز والصمم والعمى والاضطرار، إذ ما كان قائما بذاته لا يستحيل عليه قبول صفات الكمال باعتبار ذاته، إذ كل قائم بالذات يجوز قبوله للصفات، وما لا يقوم به إنما لا يقوم لقيام ضده به. ولو كان موصوفا بصفات النقص لكان محدثا، فإذا ما لا يوصف من أجزائه بكونه حيا قادرا عالما سميعا بصيرا فهو محدث لقيام دليل الحدوث به، وكون أجزاء القديم محدثة محال، وإن كان كل جزء منه موصوفا بصفات الكمال فكان كل جزء حيا قادرا عالما سميعا بصيرا لكان كل جزء منه موصوفا بصفات الربوبية، فيكون القول به قولا بآلهة كثيرة، ويلزمون بعد ذلك ما مر من دلائل التوحيد، فإن كانت تلك الدلائل صحيحة كان القول بالتجسيم باطلا، وإن كانت تلك الدلائل فاسدة، كان القول بوحدانية الصانع باطلا، وقد ثبت وحدانية الصانع بالدلائل الموجبة للعلم الثابت على طريق التيقن، فكان القول بالتجسيم باطلا. وجاء من هذا أن من قال بأن الصانع جسم فقد أبطل التوحيد في الذات، ولا يقال إن حياة الباري وقدرته وعلمه أزلية، ولم يثبت فيها صفات الكمال ولم يدل على حدوثها، لأنا بينا أن القائم بالذات لا يستحيل قبوله الصفات، فكان امتناع قبول كل جزء منه صفات الكمال لقيام أضدادها من النقائص، فأما الصفات فيستحيل قبولها للصفات لذاتها لا لقيام صفة البعض بها، فلم يلزم بامتناع قبولها صفات الكمال أن تكون موصوفة بصفات النقص التي هي أمارات الحدث، وفيما نحن فيه الأمر بخلافه، والله الموفق.
As for the second [proof], which is that the statement according to what they said leads to the nullification of the indication of tawhid – it is that if He, exalted, were composed, divided into parts, and divisible, each part of Him would be self-subsisting, because composition from what is not self-subsisting is impossible; and because if each part of Him were not self-subsisting, it would be impossible for the whole to be self-subsisting, so then the whole essence would not be self-subsisting, and the existence of the creation of the world from one who is not self-subsisting is impossible. And if each part of Him were self-subsisting, then either each part of Him is described with attributes of perfection such as life, knowledge, power, hearing, sight, and will, or it is not described with them, but rather only one part or some parts are described with them and not others. If not every part is described with attributes of perfection, then it would be described with their opposites from attributes of deficiency, such as death, ignorance, incapacity, deafness, blindness, and constraint – because that which is self-subsisting is not by its essence impossible to receive attributes of perfection, for every self-subsisting entity may receive attributes, and that which does not receive them only does not receive them because its opposite is present in it. And if it were described with attributes of deficiency, it would be contingent; therefore, whatever of its parts is not described as being living, powerful, knowing, hearing, seeing is contingent due to the evidence of contingency applying to it, and it is impossible for parts of the Eternal to be contingent. And if each part of Him is described with attributes of perfection, so that each part is living, powerful, knowing, hearing, seeing, then each part would be described with attributes of lordship, and so the statement about Him would be a statement about many gods. And after that they incur what has passed of the proofs of tawhid: if those proofs are correct, then the statement of tajsim is false; and if those proofs are corrupt, then the statement of the oneness of the Maker is false. And the oneness of the Maker has been established by proofs that necessitate certain knowledge in a way of certainty, so the statement of tajsim is false. And from this it follows that whoever says that the Maker is a body has nullified tawhid in the essence. And let it not be said that the life, power, and knowledge of the Creator are eternal, and He has not proven attributes of perfection to be established in them nor has it indicated their contingency – because we have shown that the self-subsisting is not impossible to receive attributes; so the prevention of each part of Him from receiving attributes of perfection is due to the existence of their opposites from deficiencies. As for the attributes, it is impossible for them to receive attributes by their essence, not due to the existence of an attribute in some of them; so from the impossibility of their receiving attributes of perfection, it does not follow that they are described with attributes of deficiency which are signs of contingency. And in our case, the matter is otherwise. And God is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is a proof against tajsim (anthropomorphism) presented by Nasafi. He begins by stating the second argument: that the claim of the anthropomorphists leads to nullifying the evidence for tawhid (divine unity). The argument proceeds by analyzing the hypothetical consequences if God were composite (mu'talif, mutabaddid, mutajazzi'). Nasafi argues that if God were composed of parts, each part would either be self-subsisting or not. If a part were not self-subsisting, then the whole could not be self-subsisting, making the creation of the world by such a being impossible. If each part is self-subsisting, then there are two possibilities: either every part is described with attributes of perfection (life, knowledge, power, etc.) or not. If some parts lack these attributes, they must possess their opposites (death, ignorance, etc.), which are signs of contingency (huduth). Hence those parts would be contingent, and it is impossible for parts of the Eternal to be contingent. If, on the other hand, every part is described with attributes of perfection, then each part possesses lordship (rububiyya), leading to polytheism. Thus, the claim of tajsim contradicts the established proofs of God's oneness. Nasafi then addresses a potential objection: that God's attributes (life, power, knowledge) are eternal and not proven to be attributes of perfection or contingency. He replies that the impossibility of a self-subsisting entity receiving attributes can only be due to the presence of opposite deficiencies; but for the attributes themselves (as distinct from the essence), it is impossible for them to receive attributes by their very nature. Therefore, the objection does not apply, and the argument stands. He concludes with 'And God is the grantor of success.'

Key Terms
صفات الكمال (attributes of perfection)
صفات النقص (attributes of deficiency)
ربوبية (lordship)
حدوث (contingency)
قائم بذاته (self-subsisting)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if God is composite, it is possible for some parts to lack attributes of perfection without being deficient.
Correction: Nasafi argues that any self-subsisting entity that lacks a perfection must have its opposite deficiency, which is a sign of contingency.

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi conclude if every part of a composite God is described with attributes of perfection?
A) Each part would be eternal.
B) Each part would be a lord, leading to polytheism.
C) Each part would be contingent.
D) Each part would be non-self-subsisting.

Key Takeaway
The assumption of tajsim forces a choice between polytheism and contingency, both of which contradict tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The argument shows that attributing independent power or lordship to anything other than Allah is shirk. In what area of your life do you find yourself treating your own abilities or resources as if they were independent sources of control? What practical step can you take today to redirect that trust solely to Allah?
?
If God cannot be divided into parts, then no part of your life is outside His dominion. Which part of your life do you most struggle to surrender to His absolute lordship? What would it look like for you to hand that area completely over to Him?
?
Nasafi's proof forces you to either affirm tawhid fully or risk shirk. Are there 'parts' of your belief or practice where you have allowed subtle associations (like relying on created means as if they have inherent power)? How will you actively guard against them starting this week?

Affirming a Body for God Destroys Tawhid
Imam Nasafi concludes that affirming a body for God negates tawhid in essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why affirming a body for God negates tawhid in essence and how the attributes of God are compatible with His oneness.

Core Idea
A body cannot be the transcendent Creator because parts imply imperfection.

Imam Nasafi concludes his argument on divine transcendence by addressing a key objection. Some might argue that since God's attributes are eternal, He is not described with attributes of perfection, but Nasafi shows that the impossibility of attributes accepting other attributes does not imply deficiency. This lesson unpacks that rebuttal and its implications for tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice that Nasafi begins with a conclusion and then addresses an objection.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the objection and response
Find where Nasafi says 'لا يقال' (it cannot be said) — that introduces the objection. Then trace his response: he explains why a self-subsistent entity can accept attributes, unlike a body.
The key distinction is between a body (composite) and a self-subsistent essence.
3
Understand the argument about attributes
Nasafi argues that attributes themselves cannot receive other attributes due to their nature, not due to deficiency. This is different from a body whose parts prevent perfection.
This refutes the idea that God's attributes are deficient because they are eternal.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Nasafi ends by saying 'فيما نحن فيه الأمر بخلافه' — in God's case, the opposite applies. Consider why affirming a body violates tawhid.
Tawhid requires that God be one and perfect, which a body cannot be.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجاء من هذا أن من قال بأن الصانع جسم فقد أبطل التوحيد في الذات، ولا يقال إن حياة الباري وقدرته وعلمه أزلية، ولم يثبت فيها صفات الكمال ولم يدل على حدوثها، لأنا بينا أن القائم بالذات لا يستحيل قبوله الصفات، فكان امتناع قبول كل جزء منه صفات الكمال لقيام أضدادها من النقائص، فأما الصفات فيستحيل قبولها للصفات لذاتها لا لقيام صفة البعض بها، فلم يلزم بامتناع قبولها صفات الكمال أن تكون موصوفة بصفات النقص التي هي أمارات الحدث، وفيما نحن فيه الأمر بخلافه، والله الموفق.
And from this follows that whoever says that the Maker is a body has nullified tawhid concerning the Essence. And it cannot be said that the life, power, and knowledge of the Creator are eternal, and that He is not established as having attributes of perfection and that they do not indicate temporality, because we have shown that what subsists by itself does not preclude accepting attributes. So the impossibility of each part of it accepting attributes of perfection is due to the existence of their opposites, which are imperfections. As for attributes, it is impossible for them to accept attributes due to their very nature, not due to the existence of a particular attribute in them. So the impossibility of their accepting attributes of perfection does not necessitate that they be described with attributes of deficiency which are signs of temporality. And in our case, the matter is the opposite. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion and an argument defending divine transcendence (tanzih). Imam Nasafi states that affirming a body for the Creator destroys tawhid regarding the Essence. He then addresses a potential objection: one might argue that God's attributes (life, power, knowledge) are eternal and that He is not established as having attributes of perfection (since perfection might imply composition) nor are these attributes signs of temporality. He answers that a self-subsistent entity (al-qa'im bi al-dhat) can accept attributes. The reason a composite body cannot accept attributes of perfection is that its parts have opposite imperfections. Attributes themselves (like life, knowledge) cannot accept other attributes because they are not subjects; they are accidental. Thus, the fact that attributes cannot accept perfection does not make them deficient—they are not subjects of predication. In the case of God, however, the attributes are subsisting in His Essence, which is not a body, so the objection does not apply. The passage ends with a prayer for divine assistance.

Key Terms
التوحيد
الصانع
الجسم
القائم بالذات
صفات الكمال
النقائص
الحدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that since God's attributes are eternal, He is not described with attributes of perfection, implying deficiency.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that the impossibility of attributes accepting other attributes is due to their nature, not deficiency. God's attributes are perfect in His Essence.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Nasafi, why does saying the Creator is a body negate tawhid in essence?
A) Because bodies are composite and thus need a creator, leading to infinite regress.
B) Because bodies are subject to imperfection and temporality, contradicting the oneness and perfection of God.
C) Because the Qur'an explicitly says God is not a body.
D) Because bodies cannot possess eternal attributes.

Key Takeaway
Affirming a body for God contradicts tawhid because a composite body is inherently subject to imperfection and temporality.

The Argument Against Literal Interpretation of Ambiguous Verses
Argument that literal interpretation of mutashabihat implies contradiction and kufr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how literal interpretation of ambiguous verses (mutashābihāt) leads to contradiction in the Quran and consequently to clear unbelief (kufr ṣarīḥ).

Core Idea
Literal interpretation of ambiguous verses leads to contradiction, which is proof the Quran is not from Allah.

This passage presents a powerful rational argument from the Maturidi tradition against anthropomorphism. It shows that taking verses about Allah's attributes literally would create contradiction between them, which is impossible for the Quran. By extension, those who insist on literal interpretation are forced into a position that amounts to clear disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to grasp the overall flow of the argument.
Pay attention to the key terms: ẓawāhir, muḥkam, mutashābih.
2
Identify the key premise
The argument begins by stating that taking auditory evidences (dalā'il sam'iyya) on their apparent meanings is impossible and impermissible. Why? Because of the clear verse 'Laysa kamithlihi shay’'.
This verse is muḥkam (clear) and not open to interpretation.
3
Understand the consequence
If one interprets other verses literally, it leads to tashbīh (similarity with creation), which contradicts the clear verse. This creates contradiction (munāqaḍa) in the Quran.
Contradiction in the Quran is impossible if it is from Allah.
4
See the dilemma for the mujassima
The passage concludes by showing the anthropomorphists (mujassima) face two disastrous alternatives: either the Quran is from other than Allah (due to contradiction), or they accuse Allah of error in making contradiction a proof. Both are clear kufr.
This is a classical reductio ad absurdum argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فحمل تلك الدلائل السمعية على ظواهرها كان محالا ممتنعا، وكذا قوله تعالى: لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ آية محكمة غير محتملة للتأويل فحمل تلك الآيات على خلاف هذه، وإثبات المشابهة بينه وبين جميع الأجسام في التركيب والتبعيض والتجزئ، والتناهي، وإثبات الحدود والجهات وإثبات المناقضة بين آيات الكتاب وفي الحمل على بعض الوجوه المحتملة دفع المناقضة والاختلاف، وبه أثبت الله تعالى كون القرآن من عنده، وثبوت المناقضة أوجب كونه من عند غيره على ما قال تعالى: وَلَوْ كَانَ مِنْ عِندِ غَيْرِ اللَّهِ لَوَجَدُوا فِيهِ اخْتِلَافًا كَثِيرًا، فالمجسمة لما جوزوا إثبات التناقض في القرآن كانوا بين أمرين: إما أن جعلوا القرآن من عند غير الله، وإما أن نسبوا الله تعالى إلى الخطأ بجعله الاختلاف دليل كون القرآن من عند غيره حيث ثبت الاختلاف، ولم يكن من عند غيره، وكلا الأمرين كفر صريح، وبالله العصمة.
So carrying those auditory evidences on their apparent meanings was impossible and impermissible. Likewise, the saying of the Exalted: 'There is nothing like Him' (Quran 42:11) is a clear verse (muḥkama) not susceptible to interpretation (ta'wīl). So carrying those verses contrary to this, and establishing resemblance between Him and all bodies in composition, division, fragmentation, finitude, and establishing limits and directions, and establishing contradiction among the verses of the Book, while in carrying them on some probable aspects there is repelling contradiction and discrepancy. And by it Allah the Exalted established that the Quran is from Him, and establishing contradiction would necessitate that it is from other than Him, as He said: 'And if it had been from other than Allah, they would have found in it much discrepancy' (Quran 4:82). So the anthropomorphists (al-mujassima) when they permitted establishing contradiction in the Quran, they were between two matters: either they made the Quran from other than Allah, or they attributed error to Allah the Exalted by making discrepancy a proof that the Quran is from other than Him, since discrepancy is established and it is not from other than Him. And both matters are clear unbelief (kufr ṣarīḥ), and with Allah is protection.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage presents a rational argument refuting the literal interpretation of ambiguous verses (mutashābihāt) that would imply anthropomorphism (tashbīh). The author begins by stating that taking the auditory evidences (al-dalā'il al-sam'iyya)—presumably verses about God's attributes—on their apparent meanings (ẓawāhir) is impossible (muḥāl) and impermissible (mumtani‘). He then invokes the clear verse (āya muḥkama) 'There is nothing like Him' (Laysa kamithlihi shay'), which is unequivocal and not open to interpretation (ta'wīl). Interpreting other verses in a way that contradicts this clear verse would imply establishing similarity (mushābaha) between God and all bodies (ajsām) in composition, division, fragmentation, finitude, limits, and directions. This leads to a contradiction (munāqaḍa) between the verses of the Quran. But contradictory verses cannot be from God, as the Quran itself states in Surah an-Nisa' (4:82): 'If it had been from other than Allah, they would have found in it much discrepancy (ikhtilāfan kathīran).' The author then applies this to the 'mujassima' (those who affirm a body for God): by permitting contradiction in the Quran, they are forced into one of two equally disastrous positions. Either they admit the Quran is from other than Allah (since it contains contradiction), or they accuse Allah of error by making discrepancy a proof that the Quran is from other than Him while it is in fact from Him, thus invalidating His own argument. Both alternatives constitute clear unbelief (kufr ṣarīḥ). The passage concludes with a prayer for divine protection. The structure follows a classic kalam argument: a dangerous consequence is drawn from a false premise, showing it leads to absurdity and kufr.

Key Terms
ظواهر (ẓawāhir)
محكم (muḥkam)
متشابه (mutashābih)
تشبيه (tashbīh)
مجسمة (mujassima)
مناقضة (munāqaḍa)
اختلاف (ikhtilāf)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Literal interpretation of ambiguous verses is valid and does not lead to disbelief.
Correction: The argument shows that literal interpretation leads to contradiction in the Quran, which is impossible for a divine scripture. Therefore, such interpretation is invalid and can lead to clear unbelief (kufr ṣarīḥ).

Checkpoint
According to the argument, what does taking ambiguous verses literally lead to?
A) It leads to affirming God's attributes as they appear without interpretation.
B) It leads to contradiction in the Quran and thus to kufr.
C) It leads to a valid understanding of God's nature.
D) It leads to denying the clear verses.

Key Takeaway
Literal interpretation of ambiguous verses leads to contradiction in the Quran, which cannot be from Allah, so such interpretation is invalid and can lead to kufr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever read a verse about Allah's 'hand' or 'eyes' and felt a sense of closeness that secretly inclined your heart toward imagining a form? How will you actively guard your heart from that temptation starting today?
?
The passage warns that allowing contradiction in the Quran is tantamount to attributing error to Allah. Where in your own study of Islam have you overlooked or explained away apparent inconsistencies rather than submitting to the clear verses? What is one step you can take this week to rectify that?
?
If you were faced with a verse that seems to suggest a direction or limit for Allah, would you be willing to trust the definitive verse 'There is nothing like Him' even when your intuition resists? What concrete action will you take today to deepen your understanding of Allah's transcendence (tanzīh)?

Interpreting Anthropomorphic Terms in the Quran
The author lists multiple meanings of anthropomorphic terms to show that only those consistent with tawhid apply to Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni theological method for interpreting anthropomorphic Quranic expressions by recognizing that Arabic terms have multiple meanings and the correct meaning for Allah is the one that preserves tawhid.

Core Idea
Anthropomorphic terms in the Quran have multiple meanings; tawhid guides which one applies to Allah.

This lesson introduces a foundational principle of Sunni theology: when the Quran describes Allah with terms like 'hand,' 'eye,' or 'side,' these do not imply physicality. The author of the passage demonstrates that each term has several linguistic meanings, and the theologian's task is to select the meaning that befits Allah and does not contradict tawhid. You will learn how to apply this method to protect God's transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four terms
Read the passage and identify the four terms discussed: yamin (right hand), ayn (eye), janb (side), and nur (light).
These are the key anthropomorphic expressions addressed.
2
Note multiple meanings
For each term, note the different possible meanings listed by the author. For example, 'yamin' can mean limb or power.
The author provides several meanings, showing linguistic range.
3
Apply the tawhid principle
Understand the principle: the correct meaning for Allah is the one that does not contradict tawhid (divine unity). Interpret accordingly.
This principle is the methodological key.
4
Examine the 'janb' argument
Look at the specific argument for 'janb' using Quran 39:56 ('negligence in the janb of Allah'). The author argues that negligence cannot apply to a limb, so 'janb' here means obedience or command.
Context excludes a literal limb interpretation.
5
Reflect on necessity
Reflect on why this interpretative method is necessary for defending divine unity and avoiding anthropomorphism.
This protects God's transcendence.

لأنه تعالى أخبر أنه خلق آدم عليه السلام بيديه والنعمة عند الجبائي مخلوق لا يخلق به مخلوق، فكذا عندهم تخصيص أحد بنعمة غير جائز، وقد خص بها آدم عليه السلام. واليمين يذكر ويراد بها الجارحة ، ويذكر ويراد بها القوة قال القائل : إذا ما رأيته رفعت لمجد تلقاه عرابة اليمين أي بالقوة، والعين تذكر ويراد بها الحفظ، وتذكر ويراد بها الرؤية، وتذكر ويراد بها الجارحة فتحمل على ما لا يناقض التوحيد والجنب يذكر ويراد به الجارحة، ويراد به الحذاء، ويراد به الجوار (والصاحب بالجنب)، ويراد به السقوط، ويراد به الأجل، ويراد به الأمر، يقال: هل تعلم ما فعلت في جنبي. أي في أمري، ويراد به الطاعة، فيحمل المذكور في الآية على ما يليق بصفات الله تعالى ولا ينقض التوحيد. يحققه أنه قال: عَلَى مَا فَرَّطْتُ فِي جَنْبِ اللهِ و التفريط لا يكون في الجارحة، إنما يكون في الطاعة والمضي في موجب أمره. والنور يذكر ويراد به المنور.
Because He, exalted, informed that He created Adam, peace be upon him, with His two hands, and according to al-Jubba'i, a benefit is a created thing that does not create a created thing, so likewise according to them, singling out someone with a benefit is not permissible, yet He singled out Adam with it. And al-yamin (the right hand) is mentioned and intended by it the limb, and it is mentioned and intended by it power. The poet said: 'When I see him, I raise (my right hand) for glory – you meet him with the right hand of nobility' meaning with power. And al-ayn (the eye) is mentioned and intended by it vigilance, and it is mentioned and intended by it sight, and it is mentioned and intended by it the limb, so it is interpreted in a way that does not contradict tawhid. And al-janb (the side) is mentioned and intended by it the limb, and intended by it nearness, and intended by it the neighbor (as in 'the companion at the side'), and intended by it falling, and intended by it the term, and intended by it the matter; it is said: 'Do you know what I did in my janb?' meaning in my affair, and intended by it obedience. So what is mentioned in the verse is interpreted in a way befitting the attributes of Allah and does not contradict tawhid. He confirms that He said: 'Over my negligence in the janb of Allah' (39:56), and negligence does not pertain to a limb, but rather to obedience and proceeding according to His command. And al-nur (the light) is mentioned and intended by it the illuminator.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage is a methodology section on interpreting anthropomorphic expressions in the Quran. The author begins by referencing the creation of Adam with God's hands, noting that according to al-Jubba'i, a benefit is a created thing that cannot create, and then argues that if the term 'hand' must be interpreted non-literally there, so must other terms. He then discusses four words: yamin (right hand), ayn (eye), janb (side), and nur (light). For each, he lists multiple linguistic meanings, showing that the same word can be used in different senses. The principle is that any attribution to God must be understood in a way that does not contradict tawhid (divine unity). For example, 'janb' can mean limb, but when the Quran says 'in the janb of Allah' (39:56), it cannot mean a literal side because negligence (tafrit) applies only to obedience, not a limb. Similarly, 'nur' means the illuminator, not a physical light. Thus, ta'wil (interpretation) is necessary to maintain God's transcendence.

العين
الجنب
النور
التأويل
التوحيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Quranic anthropomorphic terms must be taken literally, implying God has physical body parts.
Correction: The passage shows these terms have multiple meanings, and only the meaning consistent with tawhid (e.g., power, vigilance, obedience, illuminator) is correct for Allah.

Key Takeaway

Interpreting 'Created in His Image'
Nasafi offers three interpretations of a hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi interprets the hadith 'God created Adam in His image' to preserve divine transcendence and avoid anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
The pronoun 'his' in the hadith does not refer to God, saving us from anthropomorphism.

This passage addresses a potentially problematic hadith that could imply God has a form. Nasafi provides multiple interpretations, all consistent with divine transcendence. We will explore these interpretations and their theological implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the overall meaning. Notice the different possibilities Nasafi presents.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the three pronoun referents
Nasafi offers three possible referents for the pronoun 'his'. List them: the struck man, Adam himself, and God (honorific).
Each has a different theological implication.
3
Understand the honorific attribution
If the pronoun refers to God, Nasafi says it is an honorific attribution, like 'mosque of God'. Reflect on why this is necessary to avoid anthropomorphism.
This is the key point for defending tanzih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما المروي أنه تعالى خلق آدم على صورته فهو خارج على سبب يروى، وهو أنه صلى الله عليه رأى رجلا يضرب آخر على وجهه فنهاه عن الضرب على الوجه وقال: 'إن الله تعالى خلق آدم على صورته' أي صورة المضروب فكانت الهاء راجعة إلى المضروب لا إلى الله تعالى، ويحتمل أن تكون الهاء راجعة إلى آدم عليه السلام، وفائدة الحديث أن الله خلق آدم على صورته التي شوهد عليها الدنيا لم تغير صورته عند إخراجه من الجنة إلى الدنيا كما غيرت صورة إبليس، والحية، ولو ثبت أن الهاء راجعة إلى الله تعالى فتلك إضافة هذه الصورة إليه على طريق الإكرام للصورة البشرية المستحسنة المفضلة على غيرها من صور الحيوانات، كإضافة المساجد، والناقة، والعبد إليه، لا على المفهوم من إضافة الأشياء إلى العباد بل على التفضيل فكذا هذا، وكذا إضافة روح المسيح إليه تعالى على هذا.
As for the narration that God Almighty created Adam in His image, it is based on a reported occasion: that he (peace be upon him) saw a man striking another on his face and forbade him from striking the face and said: 'Verily God Almighty created Adam in his image' i.e., the image of the struck man, so the pronoun refers to the struck man, not to God Almighty. It is also possible that the pronoun refers to Adam, peace be upon him. The benefit of the hadith is that God created Adam in the image in which he was seen in this world; his image was not changed when he was taken out of Paradise to this world, as the images of Iblis and the serpent were changed. And if it were established that the pronoun refers to God Almighty, then that attribution of this image to Him is by way of honoring the human image, which is considered good and preferred over other animal images, like the attribution of the mosques, the she-camel, and the servant to Him, not in the sense understood from attribution of things to servants, but by way of preference. So this is similar, and likewise the attribution of the Spirit of Christ to Him Almighty.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage interprets a problematic hadith. The author begins by giving the occasion of the hadith (sabab wurudih): the Prophet forbade striking the face and said 'God created Adam in his image' meaning the image of the struck man, so the pronoun 'his' refers to the struck man. A second possibility is that the pronoun refers to Adam, and the point is that Adam's form was not changed when he left Paradise, unlike Iblis and the serpent. Finally, if one insists the pronoun refers to God, then it is an honorific attribution (idafa 'ala tariq al-ikram) like attributing mosques, the she-camel, and the servant to God, indicating honor and preference, not a literal likeness.

الهاء
إضافة
إكرام
تفضيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the hadith 'God created Adam in His image' implies God has a physical image or form.
Correction: Nasafi shows the pronoun does not refer to God, or if it does, it is an honorific attribution that does not imply similarity.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, if the pronoun 'his' in 'on his image' refers to God, how should we understand this attribution?
A) As a literal image of God
B) As an honorific attribution showing preference
C) As a metaphor for God's hand
D) As a corrupt narration that should be rejected

Key Takeaway
Nasafi safeguards divine transcendence by showing that the hadith's pronoun does not refer to God's image, or if it does, it is honorific.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Interpreting 'The Exalted One Places His Foot in the Fire'
Nasafi interprets the hadith as referring to the arrogant disbeliever.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi interprets a challenging hadith to uphold divine transcendence by identifying 'al-jabbār' as the arrogant disbeliever and ruling out movement for God.

Core Idea
God is beyond movement; thus hadith about placing a foot must be metaphorical.

This lesson examines a hadith that might seem to attribute physical action to God. Nasafi provides a reasoned interpretation, showing that the term 'al-jabbār' refers to the arrogant disbeliever, not God, and that a literal reading would imply movement, which is impermissible for Allah. We'll explore the textual and rational basis for this interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text slowly. Notice the key terms: الجبار, وضع القدم, النار, التحرك. Do not jump to translation yet.
2
Examine the translation and commentary
Compare the literal translation with the commentary. See how the author identifies 'al-jabbār' as the arrogant disbeliever and cites Quran 14:15.
3
Reflect on the reasoning
Why is movement impermissible for God? Understand the principle that any change or motion is a property of contingent beings, not the Creator. This is the core of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله: 'إن الجبار يضع قدمه في النار' قيل: إن المراد منه الكافر العاتي التمرد كما في قوله تعالى: {وخاب كل جبار عنيد} ألا ترى أن الوضع بعد أن لم يكن يكون محركا، ولا يجوز التحرك على الله تعالى.
And His saying: 'Verily the Exalted One (al-jabbār) places His foot in the Fire.' It is said that what is meant by it is the arrogant, obstinate disbeliever, as in His saying: {And every arrogant tyrant despaired}. Do you not see that placing, after not having been, would be a movement, and movement is not permissible for God Almighty.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage refutes a literal interpretation of a hadith that seems to attribute a physical action to God. The author explains that the word 'al-jabbār' here is not a name of God but refers to the arrogant disbeliever (al-kafir al-'ati al-mutamarrid), citing Quran 14:15 which mentions 'every arrogant tyrant (jabbār)'. The argument is that placing a foot would be a movement (tahrik), and movement is impossible for God (la yajuz al-taharak 'ala Allah). Therefore the hadith must be interpreted metaphorically.

Key Terms

وضع القدم
النار
التحرك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith literally describes God placing a foot in Hell.
Correction: Nasafi explains that 'al-jabbār' refers to the arrogant disbeliever, and the literal placement would imply movement which is impossible for God.

Checkpoint

B) As the arrogant disbeliever
C) As the angel of Hell
D) As a metaphorical foot

Key Takeaway
The hadith about placing a foot in the Fire is interpreted metaphorically to preserve God's transcendence, with 'al-jabbār' referring to the arrogant disbeliever.

Interpreting the Hadith of the Foot in the Fire
Sanusi explains two interpretations of a hadith about placing a foot in the Fire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the hadith about placing a foot in the Fire must be interpreted metaphorically, avoiding any attribution of physical attributes to Allah.

Core Idea
The foot in the Fire refers to the arrogant disbeliever, not a literal divine foot.

This passage addresses a hadith that might be misunderstood as attributing a body part to Allah. Sanusi explains that the 'jabbar' (tyrant) mentioned in the hadith is the stubborn disbeliever, as supported by a Quranic verse. He then argues that a literal interpretation would imply movement, which is impossible for Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its interpretations
Start by reading the Arabic text and its translation. Notice that the author presents two possibilities: the 'jabbar' could be Allah or the arrogant disbeliever.
The hadith is about placing a foot in the Fire.
2
Understand the Quranic support
The author cites the verse 'And every stubborn tyrant is disappointed' to show that 'jabbar' can refer to a disbeliever. This supports the metaphorical interpretation.
3
Analyze the argument against literalism
The author argues that if the foot were literal, it would imply a movement (from not having to having), which is impossible for Allah. This argument relies on the principle of divine transcendence.
Movement is a change of state, which cannot be attributed to Allah.
4
Reflect on the lesson's significance
Consider how this interpretation protects Allah's transcendence and prevents anthropomorphism. This is a key principle in Islamic theology.
This lesson connects to the broader theme of tanzih (transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله: "إن الجبار يضع قدمه في النار" قيل: إن المراد منه الكافر العاتي التمرد كما في قوله تعالى: {وَخَابَ كُلُّ جَبَّارٍ عَنِيدٍ} ألا ترى أن الوضع بعد أن لم يكن يكون محركا، ولا يجوز التحرك على الله تعالى.
And His saying: 'Indeed the tyrant places his foot in the Fire' it was said: what is meant by it is the stubborn, rebellious disbeliever, as in His saying the Exalted: {And every stubborn tyrant is disappointed}. Do you not see that placing, after it had not been, would be a movement, and movement is not permissible concerning Allah the Exalted.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage interprets the hadith 'al-jabbar yada'u qadamahu fi al-nar'. The author gives two possible interpretations: either it refers to Allah's foot (which would imply movement, impossible for Allah) or, more likely, it refers to the arrogant disbeliever. The author supports the latter by citing the Quranic verse where 'jabbar' describes a disbeliever. The argument is that if the foot were literal, it would imply a movement from not having a foot to having one, which is impossible. Thus the correct interpretation is metaphorical.

The Interpretation of Allah's Laughter
Sanusi interprets the hadith of Allah's laughter as a metaphor for His pleasure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi interprets the hadith of Allah's laughter as a metaphor for divine pleasure, using Arabic linguistic and poetic evidence.

Core Idea
Allah's laughter is a metaphor for His pleasure, not a literal attribute.

This passage addresses a well-known hadith that ascribes laughter to Allah. Sanusi, following the path of metaphorical interpretation (ta'wil), provides linguistic evidence from Arabic usage and poetry to show that laughter can mean manifestation of pleasure. Before reading, consider how the same method applies to other divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the poetic line about 'showing molars'.
2
Identify the linguistic examples
The passage gives three examples: the palm tree laugh, gardens laugh, and showing molars. Each illustrates how laughter can mean manifestation. Understand each one.
These are common Arabic idioms for emphasis.
3
Understand the poetic evidence
The poet uses 'showing molars' to exaggerate evil's appearance. The author uses this to show that such phrases are not literal. Reflect on how poetry supports the interpretation.
The poet is from the pre-Islamic era.
4
Grasp the final interpretation
The author concludes that the hadith means Allah manifests His pleasure and reward to His friends. This is the intended meaning, not a literal laugh.
This aligns with divine transcendence (tanzih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما روي أنه تعالى يضحك إلى أوليائه أي ظهر الرضا عنهم يقال: ضحكت الطلعة إذا أظهرت ما في جوفها. ويقال: ضحكت الرياض بأنوارها إذا ظهرت، ويقولون إذا أرادوا المبالغة في وصف ظهور الشيء: أبدى ناجذيه. قال القائل: قوم إذا الشر أبدى ناجذيه لهم طاروا إليه ذرافات ووحدانا وليس للشر ناجذان في الحقيقة، وإنما المراد المبالغة في ظهوره تشبيها بمن يبالغ في ضحكه أنه يظهر ناجذيه، وإذا بالغ في ذلك فكان تأويل الخبر: إظهار الله تعالى رضاه وثوابه على أوليائه.
And what is narrated that He the Exalted laughs to His friends, i.e., His pleasure became manifest. It is said: 'the palm tree laughed' when it shows what is inside it. And it is said: 'the gardens laughed with their flowers' when they appear. And they say, when they want to exaggerate in describing the appearance of something: 'he showed his molars.' The poet said: 'A people who, when evil shows its molars, they fly to it in groups and singly, and evil has no molars in reality, but what is meant is exaggeration in its appearance, likening to one who exaggerates in his laughter so that he shows his molars.' And if it is exaggerated in that, then the interpretation of the report is: Allah the Exalted's manifestation of His pleasure and reward upon His friends.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage interprets the hadith about Allah laughing. The author provides linguistic and poetic evidence to show that laughter in Arabic can be metaphorical for manifesting pleasure. He gives examples: 'the palm tree laughed' means it revealed its fruit, 'the gardens laughed' means flowers appeared, and 'showing molars' is a hyperbolic expression for extreme manifestation. The poet's verse illustrates that 'showing molars' is not literal but an exaggeration. Therefore, the hadith means Allah manifests His pleasure and reward to His friends, not a literal laugh.

الرضا
الناجذ
المبالغة
التأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah laughs literally like a human, with a sound and physical movement.
Correction: The hadith is metaphorical; it means Allah manifests His pleasure to His friends, as supported by Arabic linguistic and poetic evidence.

Checkpoint

A) Allah laughs with a literal sound
B) It means Allah shows His pleasure
C) It is a metaphor for anger
D) The hadith is not authentic

Key Takeaway
The hadith of Allah's laughter is interpreted metaphorically as the manifestation of His pleasure upon His friends.

?

The Fallacious Argument for Applying 'Jism' to Allah
Nasafi introduces the debate over applying 'jism' to Allah and criticizes the agency analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the argument that Allah must be a body because He is an agent is invalid and how Nasafi exposes the hidden corporealist agenda behind such claims.

Core Idea
Claiming Allah is a body because He is an agent is a flawed analogy ignoring divine transcendence.

In this passage, Nasafi addresses those who assert that the term 'jism' can be applied to Allah by reasoning from His attributes. They argue that in the physical world, only bodies are agents, so the Divine Agent must also be a body. Nasafi exposes this reasoning as superficial and reveals the true intention behind such claims—to conceal a corporealist theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the argument being refuted
Find the part where the opponents claim Allah is an agent and infer that He must be a body. Notice the analogy: only a body is an agent in the witnessed world.
This is a common sectarian argument from the Hishamiyya and others.
3
Understand Nasafi's suspicion
Nasafi suggests these opponents actually intend corporeality but hide it because their refutation forces them to reinterpret 'jism' as existence or self-subsistence.
This shows the importance of knowing the real motives behind theological claims.
4
Reflect on the weakness of the analogy
Consider why the analogy from the witnessed world to the unseen is problematic. The Divine is not comparable to created bodies in all aspects.
This lesson sets the stage for the linguistic proof in the next lesson.
