The Argument from the Throne's Finitude Against Spatial Location
Imam Nasafi argues that physical occupancy of the Throne implies divisibility, contradicting Tawheed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Throne being a limited body leads to logical contradictions if Allah were physically located on it.

Core Idea
If God occupied the Throne, He would be divisible—contradicting Tawheed.

Imam Nasafi presents a powerful logical argument against those who claim that Allah physically occupies the Throne. He shows that the Throne is a finite, limited body, and any physical relation to it would imply division and composition in Allah, which is impossible. Let's walk through his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Establish the premise
The Throne is a limited (maḥdūd) and finite (mutanāhī) body. This is the starting point of the argument.
Even if one questions the Throne's nature, the argument proceeds from what the opponents accept about it.
2
Consider the first scenario: God fills the Throne and extends beyond
The Karramiyyah held that God fills the Throne and extends beyond in all directions. Nasafi argues this implies division: parts of God correspond to parts of the Throne, and remaining parts are outside.
3
Consider the second scenario: God exactly equals the Throne in size
If God is precisely the size of the Throne, then each part of the Throne is met by a part of God, again implying divisibility.
4
Consider the third scenario: God is similar in size to the Throne
If God is like the Throne in size, that establishes similarity (mumāthala) between Creator and creature, which is impossible.
5
Conclude: spatial location is incompatible with Tawheed
All possible ways of physically relating God to the Throne lead to absurdities—division, finitude, or similarity. Therefore, the doctrine of spatial location must be rejected.
This conclusion reinforces divine transcendence (tanzīh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأن العرش جسم محدود متناه فلو كان الصانع جل وعلا ملأ ساحة العرش وفضل عنه من الجهات كلها كما هو مذهبهم الظاهر، لكان متبعضا متجزئا لا في كل جزء من ساحة العرش جزء منه، وفضل أجزاء أخر كثيرة لم تلاق العرش، وقد مر أن القول بتجزئه مناف للتوحيد، فكان القول بالمكان منافيا للتوحيد، وكذا على قول إنه مقدر بمقدار ساحة العرش يثبت تجزؤه فإن كل جزء من أجزاء ساحة العرش يلاقيه جزء منه، والقول بالتجزؤ مناف للتوحيد وكذا إن كان مثلا في القدر للعرش، وإثبات المماثلة بين الله وبين المخلوقات محال، وكذا كان محدودا متناهيا حيث كان على قدر ساحة العرش، والعرش محدود متناه. وكذا على قول الأوائل منهم متناه بجهة السفل، وكان من الممكن أن يكون أكبر من ذلك الحد أو أصغر.
And because the Throne is a limited (maḥdūd), finite (mutanāhī) body. So if the Creator, may He be glorified and exalted, filled the expanse of the Throne and extended beyond it in all directions, as is their apparent doctrine, then He would be partitioned and divisible: there would be in every part of the expanse of the Throne a part of Him, and many other parts would remain that did not meet the Throne. And it has already been stated that the statement of His being divisible is contrary to Tawḥīd (unity). Thus the statement of spatial location is contrary to Tawḥīd. Likewise, on the statement that He is precisely equal to the expanse of the Throne, His divisibility is affirmed, for every part of the expanse of the Throne is met by a part of Him, and the statement of divisibility is contrary to Tawḥīd. And likewise if He were similar to the Throne in size, affirming similarity (al-mumāthala) between Allah and creatures is impossible. And likewise, He would be limited and finite since He is equal to the expanse of the Throne, and the Throne is limited and finite. And likewise, on the statement of the earlier ones among them that He is finite in the direction of below, and it would be possible for Him to be larger or smaller than that limit.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage is a proof (dalīl) against the Karramiyyah doctrine that God is on the Throne in a physical sense. The argument is based on the nature of the Throne as a limited, finite body (jism maḥdūd mutanāhī). If God were to fill the Throne (or be exactly its size, or be similar in size), then He would have parts corresponding to the parts of the Throne. This would imply divisibility (tajazzuʾ) and composition, which contradicts Tawḥīd (divine unity). Moreover, if He exceeds the Throne, there would be parts of Him beyond it; if He is exactly its size, then each part of the Throne is met by a part of Him; if He is similar, that implies likeness (mumāthala) with a creature, which is also impossible. Furthermore, being limited and finite is incompatible with divine perfection. Thus, spatial location leads to multiple theological errors.

Key Terms
العرش
جسم محدود متناه
المبعّض
المتجزئ
التوحيد
المماثلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this argument denies that Allah can act upon or be related to the Throne in any way.
Correction: The argument only denies physical occupancy (ḥulūl) and spatial containment. Allah's actions and knowledge encompass the Throne without being physically co-located.

Checkpoint
What does the argument conclude if God exactly equals the Throne in size?
A) He would be indivisible and transcendent.
B) He would be divisible, which contradicts Tawheed.
C) He would be similar to the Throne without division.
D) He would be greater than the Throne.

Key Takeaway
The Throne's finitude makes it impossible for Allah to be physically located on it without implying division or similarity, both incompatible with Tawheed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine Allah's relationship to His creation, do you unconsciously picture Him as having a place or size? This lesson shows that even thinking of Allah as 'on' something implies limitation and division. Will you today, right now, repent from any imagined spatial limitations and ask Allah to purify your concept of Him?
?
The Karramiyyah thought they were exalting Allah by placing Him on the Throne, but their doctrine actually made Him finite. Have you ever praised Allah in a way that unintentionally limited His transcendence? What specific thought or phrase will you avoid from now on to ensure your worship reflects true Tawheed?

Proof that God Cannot Be in a Place
Nasafi refutes spatial location for God by eliminating all possible causes of particularization.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why, according to Nasafi, God's being in a place is impossible and is a sign of origination.

Core Idea
God's location would require an arbitrary particularization, proving it impossible.

Nasafi presents a logical proof to show that assigning a specific place to God leads to absurdity. He systematically rules out each possible reason for God's particularization to the Throne, concluding that spatial occupation is a mark of createdness. Let's follow his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation to get the gist of Nasafi's argument.
Notice the logical structure: enumeration of possibilities followed by refutation.
2
Identify the three possibilities
Nasafi considers three reasons why God might be particularized to a place: due to His essence, due to a meaning (attribute), or due to neither. Identify each in the text.
3
Follow the refutations
Examine how Nasafi refutes each possibility. Understand why essence and meaning are impossible, and why the absence of cause leads to absurd consequences.
Pay attention to the argument about the meaning being eternal or originated.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Nasafi concludes that being in a place is impossible for God and is a sign of origination. Connect this to the broader theme of divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما أن كان لا لذاته، ولا لمعنى ولا جائز أن يكون لاقتضاء ذاته لوجود ذاته فى الأزل، ولا اختصاص له بالعرش، ولا جائز أن يكون لاقتضاء معنى، لأن المعنى إن كان قديما فلم يكن الاختصاص في القديم ثابتا فانعدام الاختصاص مع قيام المعنى الموجب له محال وإن كان محدثا فقيام المحدث به محال على ما مر، وإن كان اختصاصه بالعرش لا لاقتضاء ذاته، ولا لاقتضاء معنى جاز أن يختص بجميع أجسام العالم فيتمكن من الصفحة السفلى من العالم، أو من الأرض، أو من الآبار، أو في بطون الحيوانات، وأشباه ذلك، وذلك كله محال، دل أن تمكنه في المكان محال. وهو من أمارات الحدوث، وبالله المعونة.
As for if it is not due to His essence, nor due to a meaning (ma‘nā), and it is not permissible that it be due to the requirement of His essence for the existence of His essence in pre-eternity, and He has no particularization (ikhtiṣāṣ) to the Throne, and it is not permissible that it be due to the requirement of a meaning, because if the meaning is eternal, then the particularization would not be established in the eternal, so the non-existence of particularization despite the existence of the meaning necessitating it is impossible; and if it is originated, then the subsistence of the originated in Him is impossible as has passed. And if His particularization to the Throne is not due to the requirement of His essence, nor due to the requirement of a meaning, then it would be permissible that He be particularized to all bodies of the world, so that He could be located on the lower surface of the world, or on the earth, or in wells, or in the bellies of animals, and the like of that, and all of that is impossible. This indicates that His being located in a place is impossible, and it is a sign of origination (ḥudūth). And with Allah is the help.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage is a proof that God cannot be in a place. Nasafi considers the possibility that God's particularization to a specific place (e.g., the Throne) could be due to His essence, due to a meaning (an attribute), or due to neither. He argues that it cannot be due to His essence because His essence in pre-eternity does not require a place. It cannot be due to an eternal meaning because an eternal meaning would make the particularization eternal, but the particularization is not eternal (it is a relation). If the meaning is originated, it cannot subsist in Him (as established earlier). Thus, the particularization would be arbitrary, allowing for any place, even absurd ones, which is impossible. Therefore, being in a place is impossible for God and is a sign of origination.

Key Terms
تمكن (tamakkun)
اختصاص (ikhtiṣāṣ)
معنى (maʿnā)
أمارات الحدوث (amārāt al-ḥudūth)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's being on the Throne is a literal spatial location.
Correction: Nasafi shows that any literal spatial location for God leads to absurdity, so it must be interpreted metaphorically or as a sign of sovereignty.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why is God's being in a place considered a sign of origination?
A) Because a place is originated and God cannot be in an originated thing.
B) Because it would make God subject to contingency and possibility of change.
C) Because it would imply He is divisible.
D) Because He would then be like a body.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi proves that spatial location is impossible for God because any particularization to a place would be arbitrary and impossible, making it a sign of creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you mentally picture God, do you unconsciously assign Him a location (e.g., 'above the heavens')? How does Nasafi's proof challenge that mental image? What specific step will you take today to train your mind to think of God as beyond space?
?
Have you ever felt distant from God because you imagined Him far away in a place? How does knowing that God is not confined to any place change the way you seek closeness to Him? What will you do this week to experience His nearness through worship rather than spatial imagination?
?
This lesson reveals that spatial location is a sign of being created. In what areas of your life do you still reduce God to your human concepts (e.g., trying to 'locate' His mercy in specific situations)? What concrete change will you make to submit to His absolute transcendence?

Divisibility from Filling and Measuring the Throne
Nasafi presents two sub-arguments that God being in the Throne implies partition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that if God were in a place like the Throne, He would be composed of parts, which contradicts tawḥīd.

Core Idea
God's place would make Him divisible, impossible for the One.

Nasafi begins by considering the Throne, a finite body. If God filled it or was measured by its space, He would be spread across parts, implying composition. This is the first argument showing that attributing place to God leads to an absurdity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the conditional structure: 'if... then...'.
2
Identify the two cases
Notice Nasafi presents two scenarios: filling the Throne and being measured by the Throne's space. Both lead to divisibility.
The second is introduced by 'likewise'.
3
Understand the conclusion
Both cases show that partition is contrary to tawḥīd, so place is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأن العرش جسم محدود متناه فلو كان الصانع جل وعلا ملأ ساحة العرش وفضل عنه من الجهات كلها كما هو مذهبهم الظاهر، لكان متبعضا متجزئا لا في كل جزء من ساحة العرش جزء منه، وفضل أجزاء أخر كثيرة لم تلاق العرش، وقد مر أن القول بتجزئه مناف للتوحيد، فكان القول بالمكان منافيا للتوحيد، وكذا على قول إنه مقدر بمقدار ساحة العرش يثبت تجزؤه فإن كل جزء من أجزاء ساحة العرش يلاقيه جزء منه، والقول بالتجزؤ مناف للتوحيد وكذا إن كان مثلا في القدر للعرش، وإثبات المماثلة بين الله وبين المخلوقات محال، وكذا كان محدودا متناهيا حيث كان على قدر ساحة العرش، والعرش محدود متناه. وكذا على قول الأوائل منهم متناه بجهة السفل، وكان من الممكن أن يكون أكبر من ذلك الحد أو أصغر أو أعلى من ذلك الحد أو أسفل، وكذا هذا على قول المتأخرين منهم أنه بجهة العلو فوق العرش وبينه وبين العرش مسافة وليس بمتمكن على العرش يلزم هذا، فإن من الجائز أنه كان أسفل من ذلك فتكون المسافة بينه وبين العرش أقل مما هو الآن أو أعلى من ذلك فتكون تلك المسافة أكثر من ذلك، وليس حدوث المحدثات تتعلق بقدر من أقداره، إذ لا تعلق للعقول بقدر الفاعل وعظمه، وصغره، ولا دلالة فيه على ذلك، فإذا جاز اختصاصه بهذا القدر مع جواز غيره لن يكون إلا بتخصيص مخصص، وما يتعلق ثبوته بإثبات غيره إياه كان محدثا، والقول بحدوث القديم محال، والقول به محال. ولأنه تعالى شيء واحد، والواحد لا يتمكن إلا في مكان واحد، فلو كان في مكان لكان في جزء واحد ويكون مثلا لذلك الجزء على ما مر فيكون هو تعالى على قدر جزء لا يتجزأ، وهذا محال.
And because the Throne is a limited, finite body, so if the Maker, glory be to Him and exalted, filled the space of the Throne and exceeded it in all directions as is their apparent doctrine, He would be divided, partitioned, not having in every part of the space of the Throne a part of Him, and there would be many other parts that do not touch the Throne. And it has been said that the statement of His partition is contrary to tawḥīd. Thus the statement of place is contrary to tawḥīd. Likewise on the statement that He is measured by the measure of the space of the Throne, His partition is proven, for every part of the parts of the Throne's space is touched by a part of Him, and the statement of partition is contrary to tawḥīd. Likewise if He were similar in size to the Throne, establishing similarity (mumāthala) between Allah and creatures is impossible. Likewise He would be limited, finite, if He were of the measure of the Throne, and the Throne is limited, finite. Likewise on the statement of the early ones among them that He is finite in the direction of down, and it would be possible that He be larger than that limit or smaller, or higher than that limit or lower. Likewise this applies to the statement of the later ones among them that He is in the direction of above, above the Throne, and between Him and the Throne is a distance, and He is not located on the Throne, this necessity follows: for it is possible that He be lower than that, so the distance between Him and the Throne would be less than it is now, or higher than that, so that distance would be more than that. And the origination of originated things is not tied to a measure of His measures, for intellects have no connection to the measure of the Agent and His greatness and smallness, and there is no indication in that. So if His particularization to this measure is permissible along with the possibility of another, it would only be by the specification of a specifier, and whatever's existence depends on another making it exist is originated, and the statement of the origination of the eternal is impossible, and the statement of it is impossible. And because He, exalted, is one thing, and the one cannot be located except in one place. So if He were in a place, He would be in one part and would be similar to that part as has passed, so He, exalted, would be of the measure of a part that is indivisible, and this is impossible.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage presents multiple proofs against the idea that God is in a place. First, if God filled the Throne, He would be composed of parts that are in contact with parts of the Throne, implying divisibility and contradicting tawḥīd. Second, if He were equal in size to the Throne, that would imply similarity (mumāthala) between God and creation, which is impossible. Third, if He were above the Throne with a distance (as later Karamiyya claim), the distance could vary, implying contingency and need for a specifier, which leads to origination. Fourth, from God's unity (wāḥid), He cannot be in a place because a place is one, so if He were in it He would be identical to that part, making Him finite and divisible. All these arguments show the impossibility of God being in a place.

Key Terms
تجزؤ (tajazzu')
العرش (al-'arsh)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God being 'on the Throne' means He is physically spread out.
Correction: Nasafi shows this would make Him divisible, which is impossible.

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi conclude from the two cases of God and the Throne?
A) That God is above the Throne without contact.
B) That partition is contrary to tawḥīd.
C) That God is limited to the Throne's size.
D) That the Throne is infinite.

Key Takeaway
The first argument against divine location is that it would make God composed of parts, contradicting His oneness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that Allah is not confined to any place, how does that change where you seek Him? Do you look for Him only in specific rituals or locations, or in every moment of your life? Will you commit to remembering that He is not limited by any space, even the space of your own heart?
?
The argument shows that any notion of God having parts contradicts His oneness. Is there any area of your life where you treat Allah as composed—perhaps expecting different 'aspects' of Him to act independently (like mercy without justice)? Will you ask Him tonight to purify your understanding of His oneness so that you submit completely to His perfect unity?
?
If Allah cannot be contained by the Throne, how can you think your problems are too big for Him? Will you stop putting Him in the box of your expectations and instead trust that He is beyond all limitations you imagine?

Likeness and Limitation from Size Similarity
Nasafi refutes the idea that God's size matches the Throne.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that if God were similar in size to the Throne, that would imply likeness (mumāthala) and limitation, both impossible for Allah.

Core Idea
Similarity in size makes God like creation and limited.

Nasafi now considers the possibility that God is exactly the size of the Throne. This would not only make Him finite but also establish a similarity (mumāthala) between Creator and creature, which is rationally impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Only two sentences. Notice the two consequences: mumāthala and limitation.
2
Understand mumāthala
If God equals the Throne in size, He shares a property with it, implying likeness, which is impossible.
Likeness in attributes is shirk.
3
Understand limitation
Being equal to a finite thing makes God finite, which is also impossible.
God is infinite.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And because the Throne is a limited, finite body, so if the Maker, glory be to Him and exalted, filled the space of the Throne and exceeded it in all directions as is their apparent doctrine, He would be divided, partitioned, not having in every part of the space of the Throne a part of Him, and there would be many other parts that do not touch the Throne. Likewise He would be limited, finite, if He were of the measure of the Throne, and the Throne is limited, finite. Likewise on the statement of the early ones among them that He is finite in the direction of down, and it would be possible that He be larger than that limit or smaller, or higher than that limit or lower. Likewise this applies to the statement of the later ones among them that He is in the direction of above, above the Throne, and between Him and the Throne is a distance, and He is not located on the Throne, this necessity follows: for it is possible that He be lower than that, so the distance between Him and the Throne would be less than it is now, or higher than that, so that distance would be more than that. So if His particularization to this measure is permissible along with the possibility of another, it would only be by the specification of a specifier, and whatever's existence depends on another making it exist is originated, and the statement of the origination of the eternal is impossible, and the statement of it is impossible. And because He, exalted, is one thing, and the one cannot be located except in one place. So if He were in a place, He would be in one part and would be similar to that part as has passed, so He, exalted, would be of the measure of a part that is indivisible, and this is impossible.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage presents multiple proofs against the idea that God is in a place. First, if God filled the Throne, He would be composed of parts that are in contact with parts of the Throne, implying divisibility and contradicting tawḥīd. Second, if He were equal in size to the Throne, that would imply similarity (mumāthala) between God and creation, which is impossible. Third, if He were above the Throne with a distance (as later Karamiyya claim), the distance could vary, implying contingency and need for a specifier, which leads to origination. Fourth, from God's unity (wāḥid), He cannot be in a place because a place is one, so if He were in it He would be identical to that part, making Him finite and divisible. All these arguments show the impossibility of God being in a place.

Key Terms
مماثلة (mumāthala)
محدود (maḥdūd)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God's greatness can be compared to creation in size.
Correction: Size comparison implies mumāthala, which is impossible.

Checkpoint
What two impossibilities does Nasafi identify if God were similar in size to the Throne?
A) Divisibility and change.
B) Mumāthala and limitation.
C) Origination and finitude.
D) Plurality and composition.

Key Takeaway
Likeness in size would make God like creation and finite, which cannot be.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine Allah's greatness, do you ever find yourself reducing Him to a mental image or size? How can you train your heart to affirm that He is beyond all physical comparisons, even while you feel awe? What specific du'a can you make today to ask Allah to purify your tawheed from hidden traces of anthropomorphism?
?
If Allah has no size and no boundaries, does that make His presence feel distant or near to you? How does your understanding of His transcendence affect your daily awareness that He is with you? What can you do this week to let the reality that 'nothing is like Him' change how you speak about Him?
?
The passage says similarity with creation is impossible for Allah. In what subtle ways do you still attribute human-like qualities to Allah in your thoughts or speech? What practical step will you take to eliminate even a hint of that comparison from your heart and tongue?

Variation in Distance and the Need for a Specifier
Nasafi shows that a variable distance between God and Throne implies contingency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that if God were above the Throne with a variable distance, that distance could have been different, implying contingency and the need for a specifier, which leads to origination.

Core Idea
Possible variation in distance proves God's location is contingent, requiring a creator.

Nasafi now examines the view that God is above the Throne with a certain distance. Since the distance could have been larger or smaller, God's location would be contingent on a specifier, making Him originated—an impossibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
This is a longer argument. Follow the logic: if God is at a certain distance, it could have been different, so it needs a specifier.
2
Identify the assumption
Later Karamiyya say God is above the Throne but not touching, with a distance.
3
Work through the reductio
If the distance could vary, then God's position is not necessary. It requires a specifier to choose this distance over others.
4
Conclude
Anything that depends on a specifier for its existence is originated, so this view implies God is created, which is absurd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأن العرش جسم محدود متناه فلو كان الصانع جل وعلا ملأ ساحة العرش وفضل عنه من الجهات كلها كما هو مذهبهم الظاهر، لكان متبعضا متجزئا لا في كل جزء من ساحة العرش جزء منه، وفضل أجزاء أخر كثيرة لم تلاق العرش، وقد مر أن القول بتجزئه مناف للتوحيد، فكان القول بالمكان منافيا للتوحيد، وكذا على قول إنه مقدر بمقدار ساحة العرش يثبت تجزؤه فإن كل جزء من أجزاء ساحة العرش يلاقيه جزء منه، والقول بالتجزؤ مناف للتوحيد وكذا إن كان مثلا في القدر للعرش، وإثبات المماثلة بين الله وبين المخلوقات محال، وكذا كان محدودا متناهيا حيث كان على قدر ساحة العرش، والعرش محدود متناه. وكذا على قول الأوائل منهم متناه بجهة السفل، وكان من الممكن أن يكون أكبر من ذلك الحد أو أصغر أو أعلى من ذلك الحد أو أسفل، وكذا هذا على قول المتأخرين منهم أنه بجهة العلو فوق العرش وبينه وبين العرش مسافة وليس بمتمكن على العرش يلزم هذا، فإن من الجائز أنه كان أسفل من ذلك فتكون المسافة بينه وبين العرش أقل مما هو الآن أو أعلى من ذلك فتكون تلك المسافة أكثر من ذلك، وليس حدوث المحدثات تتعلق بقدر من أقداره، إذ لا تعلق للعقول بقدر الفاعل وعظمه، وصغره، ولا دلالة فيه على ذلك، فإذا جاز اختصاصه بهذا القدر مع جواز غيره لن يكون إلا بتخصيص مخصص، وما يتعلق ثبوته بإثبات غيره إياه كان محدثا، والقول بحدوث القديم محال، والقول به محال. ولأنه تعالى شيء واحد، والواحد لا يتمكن إلا في مكان واحد، فلو كان في مكان لكان في جزء واحد ويكون مثلا لذلك الجزء على ما مر فيكون هو تعالى على قدر جزء لا يتجزأ، وهذا محال.
And because the Throne is a limited, finite body, so if the Maker, glory be to Him and exalted, filled the space of the Throne and exceeded it in all directions as is their apparent doctrine, He would be divided, partitioned, not having in every part of the space of the Throne a part of Him, and there would be many other parts that do not touch the Throne. And it has been said that the statement of His partition is contrary to tawḥīd. Thus the statement of place is contrary to tawḥīd. Likewise on the statement that He is measured by the measure of the space of the Throne, His partition is proven, for every part of the parts of the Throne's space is touched by a part of Him, and the statement of partition is contrary to tawḥīd. Likewise if He were similar in size to the Throne, establishing similarity (mumāthala) between Allah and creatures is impossible. Likewise He would be limited, finite, if He were of the measure of the Throne, and the Throne is limited, finite. Likewise on the statement of the early ones among them that He is finite in the direction of down, and it would be possible that He be larger than that limit or smaller, or higher than that limit or lower. Likewise this applies to the statement of the later ones among them that He is in the direction of above, above the Throne, and between Him and the Throne is a distance, and He is not located on the Throne, this necessity follows: for it is possible that He be lower than that, so the distance between Him and the Throne would be less than it is now, or higher than that, so that distance would be more than that. And the origination of originated things is not tied to a measure of His measures, for intellects have no connection to the measure of the Agent and His greatness and smallness, and there is no indication in that. So if His particularization to this measure is permissible along with the possibility of another, it would only be by the specification of a specifier, and whatever's existence depends on another making it exist is originated, and the statement of the origination of the eternal is impossible, and the statement of it is impossible. And because He, exalted, is one thing, and the one cannot be located except in one place. So if He were in a place, He would be in one part and would be similar to that part as has passed, so He, exalted, would be of the measure of a part that is indivisible, and this is impossible.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage presents multiple proofs against the idea that God is in a place. First, if God filled the Throne, He would be composed of parts that are in contact with parts of the Throne, implying divisibility and contradicting tawḥīd. Second, if He were equal in size to the Throne, that would imply similarity (mumāthala) between God and creation, which is impossible. Third, if He were above the Throne with a distance (as later Karamiyya claim), the distance could vary, implying contingency and need for a specifier, which leads to origination. Fourth, from God's unity (wāḥid), He cannot be in a place because a place is one, so if He were in it He would be identical to that part, making Him finite and divisible. All these arguments show the impossibility of God being in a place.

Key Terms
تخصيص مخصص (takhṣīṣ mukhaṣṣiṣ)
محدث (muḥdath)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God's location is fixed and necessary.
Correction: Nasafi shows it would be contingent, needing a cause.

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi say would follow if God's distance from the Throne could have been different?
A) That God is unlimited.
B) That God's location is necessary.
C) That God would need a specifier, making Him originated.
D) That the Throne would be eternal.

Key Takeaway
If God's location were variable, it would be contingent and require a creator, which is absurd for the Creator Himself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever, even unknowingly, imagine Allah as being in a particular direction when you supplicate or ponder His essence? How does this lesson expose that mental image as false, and what concrete step will you take to replace it with pure tawhid?
?
The argument shows that if Allah had a variable attribute like distance, He would need a creator. Have you ever attributed any kind of change or limitation to Allah in your heart? Write down one specific instance and repent from it, committing to study more about His transcendence.
?

The Unity Argument: One Cannot Be in a Single Place
Nasafi uses God's unity to disprove spatial location.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's unity (wāḥid) prevents Him from being in a place, because a place is one and He would become identical to that part, implying finitude.

Core Idea
The One cannot occupy one part without becoming like it.

Finally, Nasafi argues from God's absolute oneness. If God were in a place, He would occupy only one part of that place, making Him similar to that part and finite—both impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
This is a single sentence argument. Read it carefully.
2
Understand the premise
God is one (wāḥid). A place is also one. If God is in a place, He is in that one place.
3
Follow the conclusion
If He is in one place, He would be equal to that place's part, making Him similar and finite.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Refuting the Karamiyya: God's Greatness Does Not Imply Location
Nasafi refutes the Karamiyya's objection about divine greatness and location.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes the Karamiyya's claim that God's greatness allows Him to be on the Throne, and why their objection fails.

Core Idea
God's greatness is about majesty, not physical extent or location.

The Karamiyya argued that God's greatness enables Him to be on the Throne despite being indivisible. Nasafi exposes the flaw in their reasoning by clarifying what 'greatness' truly means. This lesson follows his logical dismantling of their position.

Guided Path
1
Read the initial refutations
Read Nasafi's dismissal of the claims that God is on the Throne and above the world based on indivisibility. Note his logical objection: an indivisible part cannot constitute the Throne or contact the entire world.
These are the starting premises of the Karamiyya.
2
Examine the Karamiyya objection
Identify how the Karamiyya attempt to escape: they say God is with one thing but on all parts of the Throne due to His greatness. Nasafi calls this nonsense.
3
Analyze Nasafi's distinction of greatness
Understand Nasafi's two possible meanings for 'greatness': physical bulk (which they deny) or majestic power (which does not multiply places). See how each fails to justify their claim.
This is the core of the refutation.
4
Apply the sultan analogy
Reflect on the analogy: a sultan's power does not make him occupy many places. This illustrates that majestic greatness does not imply spatial distribution.
The analogy is concrete and memorable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبطل أيضا قولهم: إنه على العرش لأنه جزء لا يتجزأ من العرش لا يكون عرشا وبطل أيضا قولهم: إنه فوق العالم لأن الجزء الذي لا يتجزأ لا يلاقي كل العالم فلا وجه إلى القول بكونه فوق العالم. وأراد بعض الكرامية الانفصال عن هذا الإلزام فقالوا: إنه تعالى مع شيء واحد فهو على جميع أجزاء العرش وأنه اختص بذلك لعظمته، وهذا هذيان لا طائل تحته، لأنهم إن أرادوا به العظمة من حيث ضخامة الجسم وكثرة الأجزاء فهم لا يقولون به مع أنا أبطلنا القول به، وإن أرادوا به العظمة من حيث الجلال والقدر فالعظمة من هذا الوجه لا توجب اختصاص الموصوف بها بأمكنة كثيرة، فإن السلطان وإن عظم قدره فيما بين العباد لم يختص بمكان هو أكثر أجزاء من
And their statement is also invalid: that He is on the Throne because a part that is indivisible of the Throne would not be a Throne. And their statement is also invalid: that He is above the world because the part that is indivisible does not touch the entire world, so there is no way to the statement that He is above the world. And some of the Karāmiyya sought to dissociate from this objection and said: He, exalted, is with one thing, so He is on all parts of the Throne, and He is particularized to that by His greatness. This is nonsense with no benefit under it. For if they mean by it greatness in terms of bulk of body and multiplicity of parts, they do not say it, and we have already invalidated the statement of it. And if they mean by it greatness in terms of majesty and power, then greatness from this aspect does not necessitate that the one described by it be particularized to many places. For the sultan, even if his power is great among the subjects, does not become particularized to a place that has more parts.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of two specific claims and an objection from the Karāmiyya. First, Nasafi dismisses the claim that God is on the Throne as an indivisible part of it, because an indivisible part cannot constitute the Throne. Second, He dismisses the claim that God is above the world, because an indivisible part cannot touch the entire world. The Karāmiyya then object: God is with one thing but on all parts of the Throne due to His greatness. Nasafi calls this nonsense. He analyzes the word 'greatness' ('aẓama): if they mean physical bulk, they themselves do not hold that; if they mean majesty and power, that attribute does not multiply the places one occupies. He gives the analogy of a sultan: great power does not make him occupy many places at once.

Key Terms
جزء لا يتجزأ
عرش
عظمة
الكرامية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's greatness (like a great physical object) allows Him to be everywhere or on the Throne.
Correction: Greatness here means majestic power, which does not entail spatial distribution or being in multiple places at once.

Checkpoint
How does Nasafi refute the Karamiyya claim that God's greatness allows Him to be on all parts of the Throne?
A) By arguing that greatness cannot be subdivided.
B) By distinguishing between physical bulk and majestic power; the latter does not multiply places.
C) By claiming the Throne is not a real body.
D) By saying the Throne is an allegory.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi refutes the Karamiyya by showing that divine greatness is a matter of majesty, not physical extent, so it does not imply presence on the Throne.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine God's greatness, do you unconsciously picture a large being occupying space? How does Nasafi's distinction between physical and majestic greatness challenge that image? Commit to correcting this in your understanding from now on.
?
The sultan analogy shows power does not require multiple locations. In your own life, do you equate influence with physical presence? How might this lesson change how you rely on God's omnipresence without confining Him to a place?
?
This refutation calls the Karamiyya's argument 'nonsense'. Are there any beliefs about God you hold that, upon reflection, might similarly attribute physical limitations to Him? Write down one and resolve to find the correct understanding from the Quran and Sunnah.
